PEEKING AT PLANS
Blog: I have a Dream … and San Mateo is creating a nightmare
Sadly my Dream isn’t shared by the County of San Mateo or the San Mateo City Council.
by Gerd Stieler
January 21, 2025 11:06 am
Updated January 24, 2025 11:09 am
Lorraine Motel in Memphis. Courtesy: Gerd Stieler Credit: Gerd Stieler
It’s Dr. Martin Luther King Jr. week, a great time to talk about education and Safe-Routes-To-School. Last week, we discussed that “School Choice” has nothing to do with educational opportunity but was born out of all kinds of ulterior
motives. This week, we do a reality check on our county’s Democrats. Have they been using “Equity” mostly just in pre-election slogans, or can they actually follow through after election season is over?
We will be talking about “Safe Routes To School” and “Slow Streets,” but most of all, we will be talking about the equity problem of “Bicycle Boulevards.”
“The time is always right to do what is right.” [MLK]
Time to get your program and your popcorn; this is a Drama in Four Acts.
Act 1: C/CAG is sharing the Dream
“The function of education is to teach one to think intensively and to think critically. Intelligence plus character – that is the goal of true education.” [MLK]
In 2023, San Mateo County politicians were introduced to The Dream. They were taught how their old ways were rotten and that they had to change. Apparently, the politicians that were summoned to take the equity training were Diane Papan,
Gina Papan, David Canepa, Lisa Gauthier, Davina Hurt, Karen Cunningham, John Goodwin, Stacy Jimenez, Christine Krolik, Alicia Aguirre, Michael Salazar, Adam Rak, Rich Hedges, Warren Slocum, Mark Nagales, Rico E. Medina, and a
few more. It is unclear how San Mateo’s City/County Association of Governments (C/CAG) decided that these people need the training. However, in the end, those students were explicitly mentioned in the disclaimer. We can also assume the
framework has been read and ratified by all members of C/CAG, all city managers, all city council members and all San Mateo Democrats until an opposing paper with opposing views is ratified next time. Without this process, the Equity
Framework wouldn’t be worth the paper it wasn’t printed on.
If any of the old and newly elected San Mateo County Democrats want to speak out against Equity … speak now or forever hold your peace.
Question: Can you explain the plans behind Transportation Equity again?
That is what this blog is for. So, after years and years of shirking the topic, the County finally took on the challenge of Equity and deserves our praise. Let us all look at the history of systemic racism in this county and how our county leaders
are reckoning with said sad history.
In San Mateo County and across the nation, people of color and other underserved and underrepresented populations have and continue to face persistently unequal economic, health, and quality of life outcomes. Public and private
institutions have historically contributed to these inequities through laws, policies, investment decisions, and other actions. C/CAG is taking steps to address Equity issues in San Mateo County. [C/CAG]
Can I get a Hallelujah for C/CAG, “historical inequities,” and “taking steps”?
“Equity entails removing systemic barriers and providing customized forms and levels of engagement and support for underserved and impacted communities to remedy past harms and underinvestment.” [C/CAG]
Can I get a Hallelujah for C/CAG and “systemic barriers”?
“C/CAG’s project team conducted Equity Focus Area (EFA) mapping and data analysis based on C/CAG’s program area themes, to identify social, economic, environmental, health, and quality of life inequities in the county” [C/CAG]
Can I get a Hallelujah for “Equity Focus Areas”?
“My community has been underserved and neglected. We don’t have any public parks. We don’t have bike lanes. The lighting is scarce, and some streets are extremely dark at night. Sidewalks are non-existent in some streets. The community
is dissected by two train tracks, therefore divided by those and other physical divisions.” [EFA Leader]
Can I get an extra loud Hallelujah for “bike lanes in underserved and neglected communities”?
Now we are all finally on the same page about the fact that Equity requires bike lanes in Equity Focus Areas. Amen. It looks like the County of San Mateo is finally getting it together and is really serious about equity – starting now!
… wait, wait. Starting now!
1/26/25, 9:19 AM
Blog: I have a Dream … and San Mateo is creating a nightmare - Redwood City Pulse
https://www.rwcpulse.com/blogs/peeking-at-plans/2025/01/21/blog-i-have-a-dream-and-san-mateo-is-creating-a-nightmare/
1/4
110 of 368

--- page 111 ---
Act 2: Alexander von Humboldt comes on stage
While the county was still working on an Equity Framework benefitting the Equity Focus Area (EFA) called the North Central neighborhood, San Mateo was prepared and pushed ahead. Mayor Rick Bonilla and his staff used grants from the
U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) to undo some of the injustices done to North Central by previous city councils.
In the racist past of this county, money from grants like this would often go to inner-city highways, jails or parking lots. But not this time. This time, the city promised to install bike lanes on various streets, most prominently on Humboldt
Street. North Humboldt Street leads to several schools and connects this neighborhood through the 3rd Avenue bike lanes to recreational opportunities along the Bay. San Mateo’s Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission also endorsed this
Safe-Routes-To-School project. The commission cited the health, safety and environmental benefits for the neighborhood. So, basically, it is all the good stuff we would expect from a solid bike infrastructure project.
Nothing is controversial about better health, better education, less car violence, more safety, less air pollution, less congestion, and environmental benefits for low-income children, at least not for your average liberal San Mateo Democrat. So,
in the end, then-Mayor Rick Bonilla pushed it through the council with a vote of 3:2. The two council members opposing equity for an Equity Focus Area (EFA) were council members Amourence Lee and Diane Papan – which might have been
the reason Diane Papan received the special C/CAG equity training in the first place.
“Our lives begin to end the day we become silent about things that matter.” [MLK]
Anyways, in the end, three city council members did what was right and expected of them, and Humboldt Street in the North Central Equity Priority Area got the long-promised safety upgrades. The kids finally received their equity bike lanes.
Question: Can we quickly dive into the Equity Framework, please.
Oh, sure, we can do that. So, according to C/CAG and the County Board of Supervisors, San Mateo County has several Equity Focus Areas (EFA). The North Central neighborhood is certainly one. Redwood City along El Camino Real and
Woodside Road is also one. Big parts of North Fair Oaks, East Menlo Park, and East Palo Alto are also there. All these areas are along the 101 highway and have to deal with more car violence, more noise pollution, more air pollution and
therefore higher rates of childhood asthma than other neighborhoods. Anybody attacking those areas is basically attacking Equity and promoting what is known as Systemic Racism.
All C/CAG politicians and city councils were introduced to all the numbers and were made aware of this injustice. And, of course, every present and future council member has promised to remedy this bad situation driven by systemic racism in
our city halls – at least during election season, they did.
So, what qualifies a neighborhood to become an Equity Focus Area (EFA):
Zero-Vehicle Households (15% threshold)
Low-Income (28% threshold)
People with a Disability (12% threshold)
Seniors 75 Years and Over (8% threshold)
Single Parent Families (18% threshold)
Limited English Proficiency (12% threshold)
Rent-Burdened Households (14% threshold)
People of Color (70% threshold)
From that, we can tell that the North Central neighborhood has many low-income households with no car access. There are plenty of people with disabilities and seniors who can’t or shouldn’t drive anymore. EFA means that rent-burdened
households, seniors with little retirement savings and single-parent families deserve better alternatives so they don’t have to waste all that money on vehicles.
Why this last part is so essential becomes more apparent once you consider today’s cost of owning and driving a car. A new car costs on average >$50,000, a used car >$30,000 and insurance in California is on average >$2,300, with another
adjustment coming from SB1107. The yearly cost of owning a car is now >$12,000, and the per-mile cost easily exceeds $2 for many models (source: AAA).
So just to make sure everyone gets the message: Equity Priority Areas (EPA), Equity Focus Areas (EFA), Community of Concerns (CoCs) – and whatever new names and definitions the county can invent for this – require and deserve bike
lanes.
Act 3: San Mateo County is still creating the same old nightmares
Of course, the report and the training happened way back in 2023 and before the elections. Let’s see if Equity is still in 2024 and after the election. So 2024 came and went, and just when the year changed to 2025, city manager Alex Khojikian
and the San Mateo city council made the New Year’s resolution to put more equity focus on the Equity Focus Area of North Central. Unfortunately, they are using the reverse psychology story again. They are walking back equity like they did
with the infamous Equity HOT Lanes.
Our streets are made for Transportation. That is why San Mateo’s municipal code requires 2-4 spots for cars in garages and driveways. But instead of enforcing the rules, the city manager shirks his responsibility and takes the easy route. He
thinks it’s OK to take valuable transportation space away from children and give it to the violators with cars. He wants to use more gas tax dollars to subsidize private car storage of a Home/Car Owner Association with too many cars.
“I have a dream that my four little children will one day live in a nation where they will not be judged by the color of their skin but by the content of their character.” [MLK]
In America, this kind of behavior is called Systemic Racism in Urban Planning – you know, the thing these guys promised in 2023 to never, ever do again. Plenty of solutions would focus on the bike lanes and compromise between parking and
driving lanes. What makes it very questionable is that the city manager and council did not make any strides even to consider any of those solutions. No, they seem to be aiming right at school children and working-class people and with no sign
of any remorse or ethics.
Act 4: What actually is Alex Khojikian proposing?
Alex Khojikian is proposing the same failed infrastructure that he proposed as assistant city manager here in Redwood City. He is running the same Big Bikeway Bluff city manager Melissa Stevenson-Diaz has been pulling off in Redwood
City. Redwood City’s “solutions” come with nice names like “Slow Streets” (without making them slow), “Bike Routes” (unsuitable for children or older cyclists), and “Bike Boulevards” (that have zero benefits for cyclists). But these solutions
never provide more safety.
So we in Redwood City already know that what Alex Khojikian is proposing is not safe for children.
1/26/25, 9:19 AM
Blog: I have a Dream … and San Mateo is creating a nightmare - Redwood City Pulse

Walk Bike Cupertino agrees: Class III lanes (Bike Boulevards) offer no protection at all and Class IV lanes and Class I trails offer the most.
Any responsible city manager would aim toward the right side of this picture. That is what America’s Bicycle Capital has been doing for 50 years. That is what Europeans and their Vision Zero plans are suggesting as well. Now, when a city
manager moves to the left side of this picture – there is a name for that. Whenever children in a low-income neighborhood are concerned, going left is what America calls Systemic Racism in Urban Planning. We have seen this kind of behavior
in Redwood City on Vera Avenue Bike Boulevard and Roosevelt Avenue Bike Route. In both cases old plans showed bike lanes and cycle tracks, but in the end all the kids got were “sharrows” aka “sharing the road” aka “non-infrastructure”
aka “not safe” aka “systemic racism”.
The only viable “Bicycle Boulevard” in all of America …
… is currently in Berkeley. Not on Bryant Street in Palo Alto, Morro Street in San Luis Obispo, Silver Avenue in Albuquerque, or Berkeley.
Google Maps shows the intersection of two Berkeley Bike Boulevards. Both have bike lanes, both streets have only one parking lane, and there is plenty of high-density housing in this area, too. High-density housing requires high-density
transportation options like these bike lanes.
source: Google Maps (https://maps.app.goo.gl/kMXersWEyXCGeMuF9)
After years and years of experimentation, Berkeley finally got smart and found the only solution to making their “Bike Boulevards” viable. At the intersection of Milvia Street and Channing Way, we see two Berkeley Bicycle Boulevards, and
both have nice green bike lanes now. We can see a mix of classes II, IIb, and IV, but no class III anymore. Berkeley recognized that they had to move more to the right side of the Cupertino chart to be safer.
Let’s repeat that: only real bike lanes work!
If Berkeley is saying that affluent school children and college students deserve bike lanes to be safer, then the County Board of Supervisors (BOS) should make that a county-wide rule.

​Dear Mayor Loraine and Members of the San Mateo City Council,​
​On behalf of Sustainable San Mateo County (SSMC), I would like to thank you for your​
​continued leadership and commitment to sustainability. Your efforts to make San Mateo a more​
​resilient and forward-thinking city do not go unnoticed. I am writing today regarding the​
​upcoming February 2nd decision on the​​Humboldt Street bike lanes​. SSMC’s mission is​
​centered on fostering a sustainable, equitable and healthy San Mateo County for everyone.​
​Central to this mission is our steadfast support for active transportation infrastructure. It is​
​through this lens of long-term sustainability and equity that we view the current discussion​
​regarding the Humboldt Street corridor and request you reject any proposal that includes removal​
​of any portion of those bike lanes.​
​Prioritizing Student Safety:​​Humboldt Street represents the longest stretch of bike lanes in​
​San Mateo and is a critical component of the​​Youth-Based High Injury Network​. With three​
​schools in the vicinity and approximately 10,000 students navigating this corridor, the safety​
​implications are profound. Protecting our youth as they commute to school is not just a policy​
​preference; it is a fundamental responsibility.​
​A Matter of Equity and Inclusion:​​This corridor sits within an​​Equity Priority Area​. For​
​many residents, the bike lane is not a recreational luxury, but a vital artery for commuting to work​
​and accessing essential services. In an area where a high proportion of residents cannot afford a​
​car, removing safe cycling infrastructure in favor of street parking effectively prioritizes vehicle​
​storage over the mobility and safety of our most vulnerable neighbors.​
​Climate Goals and Regional Leadership:​​The proposed removal of these lanes to install​
​on-street parking runs contrary to our shared goals of reducing Vehicle Miles Traveled (VMT)​
​and Greenhouse Gas (GHG) emissions. Furthermore, the eyes of the region—and the nation—are​
​on San Mateo. As other cities in the county look to your decision as a bellwether, removing these​
​lanes could create a "chilling effect" on active transportation projects across San Mateo County.​
​Acknowledging the Challenges:​​We recognize that community solutions are complex.​
​Balancing the needs of local residents with the safety of the broader public is a difficult task that​
​requires nuanced leadership. However, true sustainability requires us to lean into these challenges​
​by choosing solutions that foster long-term health, safety and equity for all residents.​
​We thank you for considering the long-term impact of this decision on the future of San Mateo.​
​We look forward to seeing the City Council uphold its commitment to a sustainable and equitable​
​transportation network.​
​Sincerely,​
​Sarah Hubbard, Executive Director​

From: Allison MacQueen Felder 
  
Sent: Thursday, January 29, 2026 12:24 PM 
To: Danielle Cwirko-Godycki <dcwirkogodycki@cityofsanmateo.org>; Nicole Fernandez 
<nfernandez@cityofsanmateo.org>; Adam Loraine <aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org>; Rob Newsom 
<rnewsom@cityofsanmateo.org>; Lisa Diaz Nash <ldiaznash@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Cc: Clerk <clerk@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Subject: I Support the Humboldt Bike Lanes 
 
Hello City Council, 
 
Please include this public comment in the packet for the upcoming 2/2/26 City Council Meeting. 
 
I am a San Mateo resident and support keeping the Humboldt bike lanes for the following reasons: 
The Humboldt Bike Lanes… 
 
Create a safe, continuous bike network across San Mateo, connecting homes, schools, downtowns, 
and bus/train transit as the #2 project on the San Mateo Bike Master Plan  
 
Are directly connected to the only 3 bike routes over the 101 in San Mateo (Peninsula Ave, Monte 
Diablo Ave, 3rd Ave), connecting eastern and western San Mateo 
 
Provide essential protection on a truck route where overserved speeds are 35 mph—well above the 
25mph speed limit (source: SM Dept of Public Works) 
 
Improve driver, pedestrian, and bicyclist safety on a corridor that was once the 5th most dangerous 
street in San Mateo County for all sources of travel (source: CCAG) 
 
Are widely used, with over 10,000 bike trips per month (source: SM Dept of Public Works) 
 
Enable Safe Routes to Schools for 4 schools serving 10,000+ students, including the new Fiesta 
Gardens K–8 school, the first neighborhood school in North Central in over 20 years 
 
Reduce greenhouse gases and vehicle miles traveled, key priorities for the City of San Mateo, San 
Mateo County, and the State of California 
 
Are supported by the majority of residents on Humboldt St, North Central and across San Mateo 
(source: SM Dept of Public Works) 
 
Are supported by 17 PTAs, SMFCSD board members, and the City of San Mateo Sustainability & 
Infrastructure Commission  
 
Save taxpayer money—removal would cost $1.3M+ and would jeopardize future grant funding 
 
Preserve safety—removing the middle section would create dangerous, disconnected bike lanes 
 
Further San Mateo’s commitment to Vision Zero made in 2015 and embedded into the City of San 
Mateo’s 2040 General Plan in 2024 
Please vote to prioritize safety and sustainable transportation in the City of San Mateo on February 2nd.  
Allison MacQueen

Subject: Please Preserve the Humboldt Bike Lanes 
 
Dear City Council, 
 
I’m writing to urge you to vote to preserve the Humboldt bike lanes. 
 
Removing them would waste public money already spent on planning and construction, with no clear benefit. Keeping the 
lanes is the more fiscally responsible choice. 
 
This is also about the future of our city. Safe bike infrastructure reduces congestion, improves public health, and supports 
environmental sustainability. It reflects smart, forward-thinking planning rather than doubling down on an outdated, car-
only approach. 
 
Public streets are shared assets, not private extensions of adjacent properties. The Humboldt bike lanes serve the 
broader community and help create a safer, more livable city for everyone. 
 
I hope you will vote to keep them in place. 
 
Sincerely, 
Sean 
 
 
 
 
 
Sean Schochet  
Pronouns: he/him/his
Upper School SEL Teacher

From: Tiffany F Siu 
  
Sent: Tuesday, January 27, 2026 5:05 PM 
To: City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Subject: North Central resident supporting the Humboldt St bike lanes 
 
Hello, 
 
I am a North Central resident (live at the intersection of N Eldorado and Indian Ave) and support keeping 
the bike lanes.  
 
During the spring and summer, my family and I use the bike lanes multiple times a week. We do outings 
as a family on the weekend and frequently use the bike to drop my daughter off at preschool.  
 
Prior to the installation of the bike lanes, we avoided going down Humboldt St by car. With both sides 
having parked cards and then two lanes of traffic, you could not drive down smoothly and would need to 
yield if another car was coming in the opposite direction. It was very crowded! I'd also like to call out that 
there have been too many pedestrian deaths by car recently, I truly believe visibility is a key factor here. 
When cars lack visibility, it increases the chance that a vehicle strikes a biker or pedestrian. Putting more 
parked cars on that street and keeping it two lanes will in my opinion, increase the risk of pedestrian 
injury or worst fatality.  
 
This was before I moved to the neighborhood, but I believe a bicyclist was badly injured while on 
Humboldt due to a collision from a car? Wasn't that a factor in exploring the installation of the bike lane?
 
I suggest that we look into, how do we move large vehicles used for commercial business off Humboldt 
and into permit parking. Many residents have noted that many large parked vehicles don't move often 
which exacerbates this issue. I myself have had to report many vehicles on my street that do not move 
for over 5 days.  
 
I'd also like to call out that I attended a sunstainability and infrastructure meeting in December where the 
survey results of North Central residents were shared, keeping the bike lanes was the leading option.  
 
Thank you for reading.

Hello SMFCSD Bicycle Community, 
 
The San Mateo City Council is considering proposals to remove the Humboldt St Bike Lanes, which are 
1.6 miles long, constructed in 2022, directly link to 4 schools, and indirectly support bicycle transit across 
SMFCSD schools. 
 
The SMFCSD Board of Trustees voted 5-0 on 1/23 to support a resolution in support of preserving 
the Humboldt St Bike Lanes in San Mateo.  
 
SMFCSD District PTA is leading an effort for school site PTA Associations to vote on this letter in 
support of the Humboldt St Bike Lanes. 6 PTAs have brought it to a vote and 6 have affirmed 
support of the letter (Fiesta Gardens,Sunnybrae, LEAD, Meadow Heights, George Hall, North 
Shoreview Montessori), with other schools in progress. Nudge your PTA President to bring this to a 
vote at your next PTA meeting. 
 
Sign a petition to support Safe Routes to School and preserve the Humboldt St bike lanes. 
 
Send a message regarding this topic to the San Mateo City Council, you can email them at: 
citycouncil@cityofsanmateo.org 
 
The San Mateo Council will be discussing this issue at a meeting on Monday Feb 3 at 7pm at City 
Hall (with opportunity for public comment either in person or via Zoom). Zoom: 
https://cityofsanmateo-org.zoom.us/j/88220205790?pwd=Ff2osKnCL8jnizzEQGu5hx1hLeJ3v1.1 
3rd & Norfolk Intersection safety improvements approved by San Mateo City Council 
 
This long-awaited project improves pedestrian and bicycle safety while speeding vehicle flow through 
the intersection. This intersection connects to 8 SMFCSD schools, the bay trail, creekside trail, and 
downtown San Mateo.  Great news! 
 
More information on the project 
 
Hoping it will be complete by the start of the 2025-2026 school year, but definitely will be completed by 
the end of 2025!

Dear Mayor Loraine and City Council Members,

have compassion for the residents and neighbors of North Central.  The idea that removing street parking in front 
of homes and then give residents the option of parking at the King Center, blocks away for many, and only for 
certain hours, is shameful.  
 
One cyclist and homeowner near Humboldt, suggested a much safer solution that works for All is to just make the 
entire lane a bike lane and return parking! Further stating that Humboldt is not a good thoroughfare due to its stop 
signs etc so the few bicyclist are likely local residents with short trips. San Mateo Ave/California Ave has always 
been the best for long distance cyclist with a short jog over to Delaware for the southern half of San Mateo all the 
way to Old County and beyond.  
 
Organized special interest groups should not have more say about a residential area than the people who live 
there. Please listen to the neighbors and constituents in North Central, explore other options for bicyclists, and 
restore street parking on N Humboldt St. Don’t mislead residents and say this is being considered, and then do 
nothing. Please do the right thing and make the residents of this community your priority when you are evaluating 
options to fix this problem.

From: Mike Swire 
  
Sent: Saturday, August 16, 2025 12:14 PM 
To: City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>; Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission 
<SandICommission@cityofsanmateo.org>; Alex Khojikian <akhojikian@cityofsanmateo.org>; Matt Fabry 
<mfabry@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Subject: Parking abuse in North Central (and elsewhere in San Mateo) 
 
Dear San Mateo leaders, 
 
As I am sure you are aware, many in our city are increasingly concerned about abuse of parking rules and 
courtesy, especially given that many neighborhoods have parking challenges. 
 
Please take a look at the attached NextDoor post from a North Central resident.  He noted that a high 
percentage of cars parked on Humboldt are not moved day to day.  They are only moved during street 
cleaning periods, after which they are quickly returned to their original position.  Long-term car storage 
such as this is not allowed per San Mateo law (which has a 72-hour limit).   
 
Some of the comments below the post mention other illegal behaviors that have contributed to parking 
challenges - e.g., commercial vehicles, reserving of parking spots, etc. 
 
I recommend that the City implement permit parking programs city-wide in an attempt to curb illegal and 
unneighborly car storage on our public streets. 
 
Thanks for your help in enforcing neighborly behavior on our streets, 
 
Mike Swire 
Bay Meadows resident

RE: Letter from Mike Swire Re: SMDJ article on rise in crashes in SM
Thanks, Mike, for sharing your concerns with us. We take safety very seriously as well and appreciate 
your input. 
 
I think it's important to clarify that the San Mateo Daily Journal article was misleading about collisions in 
the city and North Central neighborhood. The sourced TIMS data uses different geographic boundaries 
and includes State highway data that is not the City's jurisdiction or area. This significantly skews the 
data. For example. when looking at the official San Mateo Police Department's RIMS data: 
 
• There was a 4% decrease, not a 50% increase, in citywide collisions between 2022 and 2023. 
• There were 18 collisions in the North Central neighborhood in 2024, which is a 36% decrease, not a 
return to pre-pandemic levels. 
 
While one collision is too many, it's important to note that SMPD's data shows we are at least moving in 
the right direction. 
 
Community engagement in transportation and traffic safety issues is extremely important to us so that 
we consider all perspectives before making decisions on the best use of resources. With that in mind, 
there will be a 3rd and Norfolk bicycle improvement project action item at this Monday’s Jan. 13 Council 
meeting, and a Humboldt bike lanes study session item at the Jan. 21 City Council meeting. 
 
Thanks, 
 
Alex

Dear SM City Council, 
 
Happy Holidays! 
 
I wanted to share with you the attached article from today's SMDJ. In it, they report on the rising number 
of crashes on the streets of SM, especially in the North Central neighborhood.  
 
I am disappointed that recent actions of the Council seem to be moving in the wrong direction. In the 
past two months, the Council has prioritized City resources - staff time and taxpayer $ - in the opposite 
direction. The City is considering removing the new San Mateo High and College Park Elementary bike 
lanes, only two years after installation. As the article points out, this is in North Central, the 
neighborhood with the highest rate of traffic violence in the City, a block from the 101 onramp. In 
addition, the Council recently tabled the Norfolk pedestrian improvements, in another dangerous and 
underfunded neighborhood. 
 
Every minute and dollar that is spent rethinking the past threatens the safety of those who walk and bike 
in the future. Our PW staff is down two key people. We rely on grant funding for many safety 
improvements. We should instead be focusing our limited resources on finishing the Delaware Safe 
Routes to School Project, the Hillsdale High/Alameda safety project, the 19th Avenue Fashion Island 
project, and the dozens of others in our myriad of traffic safety plans.  
 
Thank you, 
 
Mike Swire

From: Lisa Taner 
  
Sent: Tuesday, January 27, 2026 9:31 AM 
To: City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Subject: Return Parking to Underserved North Central 
 
Dear Councilmembers, 
Appalling situations are easy to stomach when you aren’t front and center. And when you don’t live 
smack in the middle of it. 
But last night, as the sun set, chairs were dragged out to the front of City Hall for some of the North 
Central San Mateans with canes or those too old to stand. This was their rally and they weren’t going to 
miss it. The music, clapping, prayers and demands to return parking to their Humboldt Street homes was 
meant for you to hear - yet again. 
Former Mayor Claire Mack (a North Central resident), heads of a local church, members of San Mateo 
United and Indivisible San Mateo, along with the NAACP stood under the flag at City Hall seeking “justice 
for all” in support to restore resident parking. 
Imagine this happening on your street. 200 parking spaces gone. 
Below are the thoughts and miseries expressed last night from those living this reality.  Any two or three 
should prompt your decision to return their parking - even from your armchair.  
When friends and family won’t come visit you because there is no parking in front of your home… 
When you are given a “parking option” blocks away from your home at King Center, but only between the 
hours of 10 pm and 8 am... 
When you’ve had to have signs “RESTORE OUR PARKING NOW” in front of homes all along Humboldt for 
2+ years (not counting the days when someone pulls them up and throws them in the bushes)… 
When avid bicyclists agree that Humboldt as a connector to the highway in multiple places is too busy 
and dedicated bike lanes aren’t the safest option… 
When surveys count bikes that go across Humboldt, but didn’t actually use the bike lane and is counted 
as 2 bike uses for survey purposes… 
When organized special interests groups have more manpower to attend years’ long City meetings and 
Council feels pressure not to represent their own constituents… 
165 of 368

--- page 166 ---
2
When a realtor calls the City and is told parking will be restored and that’s how she sells a Humboldt 
street home… 
When your roofing contractor learns you are headed to this rally and remarks that he hasn’t seen the lane 
used since he’s been working on your house… 
When bikes that are seen riding down Humboldt are using the sidewalk and not the lanes… 
When a little girl who lives in North Central bravely steps out of the rally crowd to take a microphone and 
her words are for YOU, the City Council: “Fix it. Fix it. Fix it, now!” 
Mayor Loraine, admitting you've made a mistake is worthy of respect. You lived in North Central while 
you were voting to remove their parking.  Then you moved away and have not been immersed in the 
resulting pain. But it is there - every day. These are the people you represent. Not the out of town bike 
people. Leadership requires strength. 
All, what hurts our neighbors hurts us all.  Those of you who stepped outside last night to speak with rally 
members - Talk is CHEAP. North Central is known as an underserved area of San Mateo. Let’s not allow 
them to continue to struggle.  
Righting this now will pave the way for easier acceptance of more well thought-out bike lanes going 
forward. 
I stand with our Humboldt neighbors. 
 
Sincerely, 
Lisa Taner

From:

To: Clerk <clerk@cityofsanmateo.org>; Martin McTaggart <mmctaggart@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Council (San Mateo)

Subject: Humboldt Street Bike Lanes and City Survey Data Findings_27JAN2026 
 
Dear City Clerk MarƟn McTaggart and San Mateo City Councilmembers –  
 
The purpose of my aƩached leƩer is to formally memorialize and expand upon the public comments I presented at the 
City Council meeƟngs held on December 15, 2025, and January 12, 2026, regarding the Humboldt Street bike lanes. 
 
At each of those meeƟngs, I provided wriƩen “leave-behind” materials to accompany my public tesƟmony. Enclosed 
with this leƩer are the leave-behind materials submiƩed at the January 12, 2026 meeƟng, along with limited 
supplemental notes intended to improve clarity. All data referenced herein was obtained directly from the City through 
a Public Records Act request. 
 
Based on my review of the City’s own data, I oﬀer the following key ﬁndings. For each point below (Items 1–5), please 
refer to the corresponding leƩer reference aƩachments (AƩachments 1–5), located on pages 2 through 7 of this 
submission. 
 
1. The Claim That Zero Humboldt Street Residents Oppose the Bike Lanes Is Not Credible 
The City’s summary of its in-person community workshop indicates that “ZERO” Humboldt Street residents opposed the 
bike lanes. This conclusion strains credibility. Such a result would only be possible if no Humboldt Street residents 
aƩended the workshop. However, mulƟple aƩendees have conﬁrmed that Humboldt Street residents were present and 
did, in fact, voice opposiƟon. It is therefore not reasonable to conclude that 100% of Humboldt Street residents support 
the bike lanes—or that “ZERO” residents oppose them. 
 
2. The City Acknowledges AƩempts to Manipulate Online Survey Results 
The City acknowledges that a signiﬁcant number of online survey submissions were removed due to mulƟple entries 
originaƟng from the same Internet Protocol (IP) addresses. This conﬁrms that aƩempts were made to manipulate survey 
results. City-provided data shows that the vast majority of these disqualiﬁed submissions were in favor of retaining the 
bike lanes. Moreover, the City has no reliable way to verify the true residence of online respondents or to determine 
167 of 368

--- page 168 ---
2
whether addiƟonal duplicate submissions were made using diﬀerent devices or IP addresses. An addiƟonal red ﬂag is the 
claim that only ten (10) Humboldt Street residents opposed the bike lanes online, an outcome that is inconsistent with 
the volume of resident opposiƟon expressed through public tesƟmony, correspondence, and direct engagement. Given 
the City’s inability to authenƟcate online survey submissions, the reliability of these results is highly quesƟonable. 
 
3. Mailed Surveys Show a Clear Majority Opposed to the Bike Lanes 
The City mailed surveys to approximately 4,587 addresses in the North Central neighborhood and received 150 
complete responses. The City acknowledges that 68% of these respondents oppose the bike lanes and support 
restoring parking on Humboldt Street. Breakdown by street is as follows: 
 
66% of Humboldt Street respondents oppose the bike lanes 
 
67% of Idaho Street respondents oppose the bike lanes 
 
59% of Fremont Street respondents oppose the bike lanes 
Among the veriﬁable, address-speciﬁc responses received, a clear majority of residents across all three streets oppose 
the Humboldt Street bike lanes and want curb parking restored. 
 
4. A 3.27% Mail Survey Response Rate Is Insuﬃcient for Public Policy Decisions 
The City received only 150 responses out of 4,587 mailed surveys, a response rate of approximately 3.27%. Such a low 
parƟcipaƟon rate is widely regarded as staƟsƟcally unreliable and inappropriate as a basis for major public policy 
decisions, parƟcularly those involving permanent changes to neighborhood infrastructure. 
 
5. The “Hot Potato” Analysis Piƫng Streets Against One Another Is Not ConstrucƟve 
The City’s “Hot Potato” survey analysis aƩempts to compare or weigh the views of residents on Humboldt, Idaho, and 
Fremont Streets against one another. This framing is not construcƟve. The only meaningful conclusion supported by the 
data is that a majority of residents on all three streets oppose the bike lanes and support restoring parking on 
Humboldt Street. Framing the analysis in a way that pits neighbors against one another distracts them from this clear 
and consistent outcome. 
 
I respecƞully request that the Council reconsider its reliance on ﬂawed and unreliable survey interpretaƟons and give 
appropriate weight to the City’s own veriﬁable data, as well as to the sustained and documented opposiƟon from 
directly impacted residents. 
 
Thank you for your Ɵme and consideraƟon. 
Taso Zografos, San Mateo Resident

San Mateo United Homeowners Association (SMUHA), Members, and Residents 
 
FROM:  Taso Zografos, San Mateo City Resident 
 
 
 
REGARDING:   Humboldt Street Bike Lanes and City Survey Data Findings 
The purpose of this letter is to formally memorialize and expand upon the public comments I 
presented at the City Council meetings held on December 15, 2025, and January 12, 2026, 
regarding the Humboldt Street bike lanes. 
At each of those meetings, I provided written “leave-behind” materials to accompany my public 
testimony. Enclosed with this letter are the leave-behind materials submitted at the January 12, 
2026 meeting, along with limited supplemental notes intended to improve clarity. All data 
referenced herein was obtained directly from the City through a Public Records Act request. 
Based on my review of the City’s own data, I offer the following key findings. For each point below 
(Items 1–5), please refer to the corresponding reference attachments (Attachments 1–5), located 
on pages 2 through 7 of this submission. 
 
1. The Claim That Zero Humboldt Street Residents Oppose the Bike Lanes Is Not Credible 
The City’s summary of its in-person community workshop indicates that “ZERO” Humboldt Street 
residents opposed the bike lanes. This conclusion strains credibility. 
Such a result would only be possible if no Humboldt Street residents attended the workshop. 
However, multiple attendees have confirmed that Humboldt Street residents were present and did, 
in fact, voice opposition. It is therefore not reasonable to conclude that 100% of Humboldt Street 
residents support the bike lanes—or that “ZERO” residents oppose them. 
 
2. The City Acknowledges Attempts to Manipulate Online Survey Results 
The City acknowledges that a significant number of online survey submissions were removed due 
to multiple entries originating from the same Internet Protocol (IP) addresses. This confirms that 
attempts were made to manipulate survey results. 
City-provided data shows that the vast majority of these disqualified submissions were in favor of 
retaining the bike lanes. Moreover, the City has no reliable way to verify the true residence of online 
respondents or to determine whether additional duplicate submissions were made using different 
devices or IP addresses. 
An additional red flag is the claim that only ten (10) Humboldt Street residents opposed the bike 
lanes online, an outcome that is inconsistent with the volume of resident opposition expressed 
169 of 368

--- page 170 ---
Continued 
 
Taso Zografos Letter to San Mateo City Council RE Humboldt St. Bike Lanes 27JAN2026 
Page 2 | 7 
through public testimony, correspondence, and direct engagement. Given the City’s inability to 
authenticate online survey submissions, the reliability of these results is highly questionable. 
 
3. Mailed Surveys Show a Clear Majority Opposed to the Bike Lanes 
The City mailed surveys to approximately 4,587 addresses in the North Central neighborhood and 
received 150 complete responses. The City acknowledges that 68% of these respondents oppose 
the bike lanes and support restoring parking on Humboldt Street. 
Breakdown by street is as follows: 
• 
66% of Humboldt Street respondents oppose the bike lanes 
• 
67% of Idaho Street respondents oppose the bike lanes 
• 
59% of Fremont Street respondents oppose the bike lanes 
Among the verifiable, address-specific responses received, a clear majority of residents across all 
three streets oppose the Humboldt Street bike lanes and want curb parking restored. 
 
4. A 3.27% Mail Survey Response Rate Is Insufficient for Public Policy Decisions 
The City received only 150 responses out of 4,587 mailed surveys, a response rate of 
approximately 3.27%. Such a low participation rate is widely regarded as statistically unreliable. 
 
5. The “Hot Potato” Analysis Pitting Streets Against One Another Is Not Constructive 
The City’s “Hot Potato” survey analysis attempts to compare or weigh the views of residents on 
Humboldt, Idaho, and Fremont Streets against one another. This framing is not constructive. 
The only meaningful conclusion supported by the data is that a majority of residents on all three 
streets oppose the bike lanes and support restoring parking on Humboldt Street. Framing the 
analysis in a way that pits neighbors against one another distracts them from this clear and 
consistent outcome. 
I respectfully request that the Council reconsider its reliance on flawed and unreliable survey 
interpretations and give appropriate weight to the City’s own verifiable data, as well as to the 
sustained and documented opposition from directly impacted residents. 
Thank you for your time and consideration. 
Taso Zografos, San Mateo Resident

FW: San Mateo needs a safe bicycle system for our kids and families
From: Annie Tsai 
 
Sent: Thursday, January 23, 2025 11:12:48 PM 
To: Rob Newsom <rnewsom@cityofsanmateo.org>; Lisa Diaz Nash <ldiaznash@cityofsanmateo.org>; Adam Loraine 
<aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org>; Danielle Cwirko-Godycki <dcwirkogodycki@cityofsanmateo.org>; Nicole Fernandez 
<nfernandez@cityofsanmateo.org>; Alex Khojikian <akhojikian@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Subject: San Mateo needs a safe bicycle system for our kids and families  
  
Good evening Mayor Newsom, Deputy Mayor Loraine, Council members Diaz Nash, Cwirko-Godycki and 
Fernandez, and City Manager Khojikian, 
 
I’m writing to express my strong support for San Mateo prioritizing a safe and comprehensive bicycle 
system, particularly for our youngest residents and families. This letter specifically pertains to the 
upcoming discussions about whether to downgrade existing safety measures along Humboldt Street in 
North Central San Mateo. 
 
Before these safety measures were implemented, this stretch of road represented not only the city’s 
longest part of the "connected system" in San Mateo but also one of the most dangerous stretches for 
bicyclists. At a minimum, I urge the City to maintain the current levels of safety. 
 
North Central has a higher population density than most parts of San Mateo, with significant traffic from 
cars and large trucks servicing nearby business centers. Removing existing safety measures will 
undoubtedly increase the risk of accidents and injuries. With the string of near misses, injuries, and 
fatalities involving pedestrians, cyclists, and vehicles in our city over these last few years, we cannot 
afford to take steps backward. Any reduction in safety measures in a known accident hot spot would not 
only endanger lives but also increase liability for the City. 
 
As a parent of a child who bikes to and from school every day, I acutely understand the importance of 
safe streets. My son’s route includes quiet, open streets and almost entirely protected bike lanes on the 
busy streets, which allow him to ride safely as part of a “bike bus” with other kids. This bike bus replaces 
five cars on the road, two trips a day, five days a week—amounting to up to 50 fewer car rides weekly in 
an already congested area. Without bike lanes, these trips would shift to cars, further exacerbating traffic 
issues in Shoreview, Parkside, and beyond.  
 
None of the parents in our bike bus started out thinking that cycling was going to be a realistic option, but 
it was dedicated bicycle lanes that convinced us to try. This is how we get more cars off the road and 
reduce traffic - by giving residents a viable alternative. 
 
I respectfully urge you to vote in favor of retaining Humboldt Street’s current configuration or adopting an 
alternative design that preserves existing levels of bicycle safety. As the largest city in the county, San 
Mateo should lead the way in building a safe and comprehensive bicycle system for all residents.

Thank you for considering this vital issue. 
 
Kind regards, 
Annie Tsai

From: United San Mateo 
 
Sent: Tuesday, January 27, 2026 9:06:47 PM 
To: City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Subject: Call to Action: Immediate Return of North Central Parking  
  
Dear Council Members,  
 
I am requesting immediate removal of bike lanes and return of street parking to the homes on Humboldt 
Street. Last night at the rally in front of City Hall, it was brought to my attention that North Central San 
Mateans are still suffering from the city's decision to remove valuable street parking and replace them 
with highly underutilized bike lanes. 
 
As humans with a fundamental need for socialization to support essential psychological and physical 
health, it is incomprehensible the city has instituted a physical barrier preventing and discouraging 
family and friends from visiting loved ones on Humboldt Street. Even worse, the barrier has lingered for 
over two years without the city's commitment and action to remedy the mistake despite repeated pleas 
from residents including a former mayor.  
 
As Council Members, you promoted Measure T as the answer to claims that seniors were being pushed 
out of San Mateo. Given that pleas for the return of parking on Humboldt Street have been ignored, it 
appears the messaging was a promotional point rather than a reflection of true caring for seniors. As 
humans, we're physiologically programmed to deteriorate as we age. Some degree of physical 
compromise is inevitable. It's unconscionable that seniors and handicapped residents along with their 
service providers are forced to park a fair distance away from their homes. The City of San Mateo proudly 
displays the WHO's Age-Friendly City designation although its years of inaction loudly professes 
otherwise. 
 
I cannot imagine the replacement of street parking with bike lanes happening in the most affluent areas 
of the city. With the NAACP supporting the voices of the Humboldt Street residents, I now wonder if the 
exploration to implement the flawed bike lanes in other areas of the city is really meant to dilute 
geographic discrimination. With traffic along Alameda De Las Pulgas coming from the homes, schools, 
churches, recreation centers, and a shopping mall (with more homes and offices to be added), it's 
unfathomable that this main artery originating from Menlo Park and running through the back of the city 
would be reduced to one lane in order to accomodate a separate bike lane.

From:
Jake Adger 
Sent:
Monday, February 2, 2026 9:20 AM
To:
dciwkogdycki@cityofsanmateo.org; Nicole Fernandez; Adam Loraine; 
rnewson@cityofsanmateo.org; jdiaznash@cityofsanmateo.org
Cc:
Clerk; City Council (San Mateo)
Subject:
Please keep the Humboldt st bike lanes
Dear Mayor and City Council Members, 
I’m a San Mateo resident, and I’m writing to ask you to please vote to keep the Humboldt st. bike lanes. I 
had a severe bicycle accident 5 years ago just two blocks from my home in San Mateo, so safety is a very 
personal issue for me. 
The Humboldt bike lanes are a critical part of a safe, continuous bike network across San Mateo. They 
connect homes, schools, downtown areas, and bus and train transit, and they’re identified as the #2 
priority project in the San Mateo Bike Master Plan. Just as importantly, Humboldt st. connects directly to 
the only three bike routes over 101 in San Mateo (Peninsula Ave, Monte Diablo Ave, and 3rd Ave), making 
it a key link in the city. 
Safety is a big reason I support keeping them. Humboldt is a truck route where observed speeds average 
around 35 mph—well above the 25 mph speed limit. Before these improvements, this corridor was one 
of the most dangerous streets in San Mateo County for all users. The bike lanes add essential protection 
not just for people biking, but also for pedestrians and drivers. 
The lanes are also clearly being used. There are more than 10,000 bike trips per month on Humboldt, 
which shows that this isn’t a theoretical improvement—it’s serving real people every day. 
They’re especially important for families. The Humboldt bike lanes enable Safe Routes to Schools for 
four schools serving over 10,000 students, including the new Fiesta Gardens K–8 school—the first 
neighborhood school in North Central in more than 20 years. 
Beyond safety and access, keeping the bike lanes supports goals the city has already committed to: 
reducing greenhouse gas emissions and vehicle miles traveled, and advancing Vision Zero. Removing the 
middle section would break up the network and create dangerous, disconnected bike lanes, 
undermining those goals. 
There’s also a practical, financial angle. Removing the bike lanes would cost taxpayers more than $1.3 
million and could jeopardize future grant funding. That’s a lot of money to spend to make the street less 
safe and less functional. 
I respectfully ask you to vote to prioritize safety and sustainable transportation by keeping the Humboldt 
st. bike lanes. 
Thank you for your time and for your service to our community.

2
Sincerely, 
Jake Adger 
San Mateo

January 30, 2026 
 
 
Mayor Adam Loraine and members of the San Mateo City Council 
San Mateo City Hall 
330 West 20th Avenue 
San Mateo, CA 94403 
 
Re: February 2, 2026 agenda item no. 7  
Please move forward with Humboldt bike lanes Alternative no. 2 
Dear Mayor Lorraine and Council members: 
Climate Action California is a grassroots climate advocacy group with more than 7,000 supporters 
around the state, all concerned about the adverse impacts of global heating on our planet. On behalf of 
our Transportation Team, I write in support of keeping the Humboldt Street bike lanes (City Council 
Agenda Item no. 7, February 2, 2026 regular meeting). Specifically, we support Alternative 2, “Keep-As-Is 
with Additional Humboldt Street Calming Measures + Streetlighting Upgrades + Explore Permit Parking 
Program.” 
Transportation is the largest single source of climate-warming emissions in California, responsible for 
over 38 percent of the state’s total emissions and over 50 percent of emissions in San Mateo County. 
More than 70 percent of trips in San Mateo County are currently taken by solo drivers. Along with 
vehicle electrification, reduction of vehicle miles traveled (VMT) is a vital part of the state’s strategy to 
reduce transportation emissions. The California Air Resources Board (CARB) has set a target of reducing 
VMT 24 percent below 2001 levels by 2030, and 29 percent below 2001 levels by 2045.  
Reducing VMT to meet our state’s goals can be achieved only if we enhance both public transportation 
and active transportation, including bicycling. Removing bike lanes to restore street parking to 
Humboldt Street would encourage even more solo driving and run counter to the state’s emissions and 
VMT reduction targets. Keeping the Humboldt Street bike lanes and making them safer with the 
addition of traffic calming measures and better lighting will encourage more biking on this important 
street. Addressing businesses’ concerns by exploring parking permits should address at least some of the 
concerns about lost parking spaces.  
198 of 368

--- page 199 ---
The transition to low-emissions transportation is going to require all of us to make changes in our lives
and routines. Council action to encourage active transportation and add parking permits to the
commercial area are both measures that will ease the inevitable change.

Please instruct staff to work on Alternative 2. We look forward to participating in the Council’s further
deliberations on this subject.

Sincerely,

Janet Cox
CEO
Climate Action California

2 Feb 2026 Council Meeting Agenda Item #7 Humboldt Bike Lanes Alternative
Honorable Members of the San Mateo City Council, 
 
Regarding the pending decisions about the Humboldt Street bike lanes, I encourage you to consider the 
following carefully. 
 
As much of a squabble as this issue has been, in a broader view it is not about bikes and parking places. It is 
about who controls narratives to get what they want from the city. 
 
Although I am President and CEO of Ethics San Mateo, a California Nonprofit Public Benefit corporation, and 
there potentially are some ethical issues in the proceedings and alliances, I am writing this as an individual.  
 
I am not going to state whether I support or oppose either the removal of the bike lanes and restoration of street 
parking on Humboldt. Why? Because I do not live in North Central and I don’t ride a bike in that area. The 
residents of North Central, especially those on Humboldt and surrounding streets, are the people who feel the 
impact from the lack of parking, not me, and certainly not the special interests. The thoughts of people who 
actually ride a bicycle on Humbolt are to be considered. When representatives and members of bicycle special 
interest groups call for a mass biking demonstration, or when posing for a staged newspaper picture, that so-
called proof of bike lane usage cannot be considered. When on the day of official surveys by the city, there is a 
huge surge of bikes reported without apparent reason, it smells of manipulation, perhaps a leak of information 
about the date of the survey? You must ignore data which is demonstrably flawed. Come on, some supporters of 
the bike lanes have stated there are 10,000 bike trips per month. Get real. 
 
I do care about this because it is a clear case of not considering residents’ voices as being most important. It is 
about loud voices of special interests trying to control a narrative. We have seen this scenario over and over. It 
is time to put a stop to the subrogation of our residents in favor of big money interests. Time to stop the political 
shenanigans in using this as a rally cry by those seeking support for the next election.  
 
I remind you of an Ethics Watch published by Ethics San Mateo on March 30, 2023, detailing council’s 
discussion and facts regarding the bike lanes. The then-members of the city council agreed mistakes were made 
that had to be remedied. Three years later the city has accomplished nothing, except spending staff time, money 
and causing divisive conversations.  
 
Since the early days of the debates over these bike lanes the pile-on of politicians, and the special interest 
groups of which they seek approval, has become a painful scrum to the residents of North Central. The 
demographics of the neighborhood tell the story. Just look at the census tract data. In 2019 70% of householders 
were non-white. The population was over 7,700 and there was a median income of just over $24,000. That is 
200 of 368

--- page 201 ---
2
about $30,000 in 2026-dollar spending power with inflation. 
(https://datacommons.org/place/geoId/06081606200) 
 
North Central is an Equity Priority Neighborhood. That’s why the HUD Community Development Block Grant 
Program exists. It is to right a wrong, the lack of investment in these underserved neighborhoods, not to 
provide a bike lane for special interest groups to tout as a win. 
 
As a reminder, and for clarification for those who do not understand the meaning of the designation, an Equity 
Priority Neighborhood is a specific geographic area identified by planners as having a high concentration of 
underserved populations, including low-income households and people of color, who have historically faced 
disinvestment. Have you lost sight of this? Do you want to appear to be turning a blind eye, as your 
predecessors a century ago did? 
 
If, indeed, the lives of the residents of North Central were improved overall by the bike lanes, I doubt if this 
fevered debate would be taking place. If children were observed filling the lanes before and after school, it 
would be great. If on any given day, with good weather, families could be seen in mass enjoying a ride, I would 
suppose, in the words of a City of San Mateo Sustainability and Infrastructure Commissioner, the 
“inconvenienced” residents just might have a more temperate tone.  
 
The studies, surveys and purported observations by city staff simply make no sense. I have heard from people 
who live in North Central, or travel consistently on Humbolt, or have firsthand knowledge, or have recorded the 
bike lane traffic. I have listened to the supporters of the bike lanes. I have driven the length of the Humboldt 
Street bike lanes a number of times on good weather days at various times and have seen no more than three 
bicycles. On one occasion, one of two were on the sidewalk. Yes, my observations were a very small sampling, 
but if one were to believe the astronomical number of bicyclists using the lanes that are being touted, I certainly 
would have seen more than two or three. 
 
The opponents and supporters of the restoration of parking, a potential loss of bike lanes, bring many 
arguments. I see a lot of distractions. No one will argue that any injury or death for ANY reason or means is not 
sad or tragic for any avoidable traffic incident, especially when resulting in a death. Accusing those who want 
restoration of parking as not caring about injuries or deaths is a heartless tactic to gain sympathy for their cause. 
It is as cold-blooded telling disabled and elderly people that having to park blocks away from their home is a 
mere “inconvenience.” It is also simply inhumane to use any tragic event for political purposes. It, however, 
seems to be a “go-to” for those pushing their agendas and ideology.  
 
North Central is an example of a failure to plan for future growth. Over 8,000 people live in an area that was 
designed for lifestyles and the day-to-day activities of the 1940’s and 50’s. The special interest groups, as well 
as city officials and staff, need to stop blaming the residents for a problem they did not create. Some have two 
families living in their houses, a fact that some use for an argument of why parking is an issue - yet the city is 
encouraging ADUs so more people can live on a single R1 lot. Please say goodbye to that argument, and the 
cultural/racial overtones it carries.  
 
It is also an area where, in time past, minority residents were concentrated due to unfair, racist, and simply 
abhorrent acts of lenders and developers aided by our local governments by their turning a blind eye to the 
201 of 368

--- page 202 ---
3
discrimination. This undoubtedly led to the conditions warranting the current designation of an Equity Priority 
Designation even with the elimination of the previous exclusionary and cruel policies. 
 
Street parking is NOT “Free Parking.” Residents pay taxes that provide for roadways that accommodate curb 
parking. The arguments using statements that residents are just trying to get “Free Parking” must be ignored. It 
is only one of many distractions from the real issue. If any neighborhood deserves street parking, it is North 
Central. Again, this area was not built to accommodate the modern-day requirements imposed on many of the 
residents. Using them as pawns in a power struggle is unacceptable. The removal of the bike lanes on Humbolt 
does not constitute a loss of anything to all but a few people who might be slightly inconvenienced by having to 
take alternative, perhaps safer, routes while riding. The residents of North Central can easily show the harm and 
losses caused by the removal of parking. And PLEASE do not try to accuse me of not caring about tragic 
events. I am the very last person that could be considered callous. I have risked my life for others many, many 
times.

election cycle begins? A compromise makes no one whole. The discontent of even a partial loss causes nothing 
but a drive to take on the battle again. Reference the remarks made by former members of the City Council 
regarding the passage of Measure Y a few years ago. “We will continue to fight” is a quote from a video that is 
widely available. They promised to continue the fight against the principles of the voter passed mandate, and 
guess what – they finally won with Measure T. Councilmembers, remember that as the North Central 
neighborhood becomes more and more unlivable because of outside interests. 
 
Do you really believe this vociferous battle is over a few blocks of green paint? No, it certainly is not. It is about 
the power of big money and special interests working to conquer the underserved neighborhoods, or anywhere 
they desire to profit from. It is about them growing in strength and influence with each win. It is about who can 
manipulate the city for their benefit. 
 
Are you going to vote to show you put the voices and needs of actual residents first, to protect seniors, disabled, 
and working-class residents or will you vote to get support from those who do not care about them for your next 
election? 
 
Why, if I don’t oppose or support the restoration of parking, am I asking you this? Well, I figure once a 
politician makes it known their re-election is more important than their constituency, we’re all in trouble. 
 
Dave Cohen

Pedestrian and cyclist safety is paramount; cities across the Peninsula are witnessing a sharp increase

the City Council should affirm the importance of safe bike routes in the region. While bike boulevards 
sound like a viable option in theory, in reality they do little to slow traffic or discourage aggressive, 
dangerous driving habits. I encourage the City Council to instead explore a residential parking permit 
program for the North Central neighborhood to deter frequent long-term and commercial parking on city-
owned streets. Finally, spending roughly $1.5 million to dismantle critical safety infrastructure is not a 
fiscally prudent move. As the City Council prepares to ask residents for a quarter-cent sales tax increase 
this November, this bike lane vote serves as a referendum on our leadership’s fiscal stewardship of 
limited taxpayer resources.

San Mateo City Council, 
Let's Change our Priorities 
 
City Council must act this Monday, February 2, not by investing new funds 
in Humboldt bike-lanes redesign measures for our North Central 
neighborhood, but, instead by changing focus to: 
 
1) Stripe locations of parking spaces on streets near Humboldt's bike-
lanes; 
 
 
2) Protect pedestrians and cyclists. Enforce the the State-required safety 
distance at intersections near Humboldt. Fund daytime towing, in addition 
to ticketing; 
 
3) Tow chronically-unmoved vehicles near Humboldt, such vehicles that 
are now either ticketed on street-sweeping days, or are ignored by City-
contracted enforcement personnel; 
 
4) Concentrate future funding on streets where bicyclists and speeding 
two-wheeled motorized vehicles already travel, such as on Monte Diablo 
Avenue near Humboldt; 
 
5) Install “Walk-bicycles” enforcement signing for the entrances to the 
Monte Diablo/Highway 101 pedestrian over-crossing to protect senior 
walkers on the ramps from bicyclists and motorized vehicles that are 
already using that route to access neighborhoods easterly of Bayshore 
Freeway. 
 
One hopes future City Councils will realize that by replacing street parking 
with bike-lanes, the well-meaning City causes many residents to pave over 
water-catching turf areas in order to continue to meet their parking needs.

this paving will necessitate costly infrastructure improvements, necessary 
to protect residents from additional flooding. 
 
And, more water will raise the levels of the Bay and lead to even more 
frequent dredging there. 
 
Council, please do not defer action on urgent community requests. Please 
re-focus funding now. 
 
Doug Handerson 
San Mateo, CA

protect our residents, particularly those who don't or can't drive. Voting to remove the Humboldt bike

vulnerable community members. Please retain the Humboldt bike lanes. Please expand our network of 
safe bike lanes in San Mateo. Please prioritize pedestrian safety improvements.

City's climate commitments. We must chip away at GHGs emissions from transportation - the largest 
source of GHGs in our City, to meet our Climate Action Plan's targets.  
 
Please do the right thing for public safety, equity and the climate and retain the Humboldt bike lanes.

Bike Lanes and North Central
Dear City Council, 
 
I am advocating for a return of parking to the North Central Residents. This issue is 
one that will likely impact a lot of other neighborhoods in the future as well. Lets take a 
hard look at the future of San Mateo and what’s best for the whole community. The 
piece below looks at the direction the City is heading:  
 
Bike Lane Controversy: Ideology vs Common Sense 
 
There has been a push by the city of San Mateo to add bike lanes by reducing or 
replacing car lanes and/or parking with bike lanes: This happened in North Central 
along Humboldt and Poplar; now, along 19th Avenue and Fashion Island Blvd. a 
second car lane would be precluded; and another project along Delaware could 
negatively impact congestion.  
 
The facts: The number of households with 2 or more cars has increased substantially 
from 22% in 1960 to 60% in 2023 and there are 40,000 households. Thirteen large 
development proposals have been submitted in San Mateo including the partial 
Hillsdale Shopping demolition adding 1392 housing units; The Concar/Delaware 
redevelopment adding 869 housing units; a 14 story building on Fourth and El Camino 
with 236 residential units. This Means a lot more cars on the road.  
 
Less than 1% of San Mateo’s population rides bicycles as a form of transportation and 
commuting in lieu of cars and this has not increased in 20 years even with adding bike 
paths. How often do you see bike riders including recreation bikers and in large 
numbers? This is not San Francisco.

and more bike lanes, but I doubt that will seriously encourage more transportation

small number of bikers while compromising traffic and parking makes no sense. At 
some point, it is really the responsibility of bikers to watch out for their own safety, not 
the city. 
 
BTW, I am a bike rider.

Clerk; City Council (San Mateo)
Subject:
I support keeping the Humboldt Bike Lanes
Hi City Council, 
 
Please include this public comment in the packet for the upcoming 2/2/26 City Council Meeting. 
 
I am a San Mateo resident and support keeping the Humboldt bike lanes for the following reasons: 
 
The Humboldt Bike Lanes: 
 
 
Create a safe, continuous bike network across San Mateo, connecting homes, schools, 
downtowns, and bus/train transit as the #2 project on the San Mateo Bike Master Plan 
 
Are directly connected to the only 3 bike routes over the 101 in San Mateo (Peninsula Ave, Monte 
Diablo Ave, 3rd Ave), connecting eastern and western San Mateo 
 
Provide essential protection on a truck route where over served speeds are 35 mph- well above 
the 25mph speed limit (source: SM Dept of Public Works) 
 
Improve driver, pedestrian, and bicyclist safety on a corridor that was once the 5th most 
dangerous street in San Mateo County for all sources of travel (source: CCAG) 
 
Are widely used, with over 10,000 bike trips per month (source: SM Dept of Public Works) 
 
Enable Safe Routes to Schools for 4 schools serving 10,000+ students, including the new Fiesta 
Gardens K-8 school, the first neighborhood school in North Central in over 20 years 
 
Reduce greenhouse gases and vehicle miles traveled, key priorities for the City of San Mateo, San 
Mateo County, and the State of California 
 
Are supported by the majority of residents on Humboldt St, North Central and across San Mateo 
(source: SM Dept of Public Works) 
 
Are supported by 17 PTSs, SMFCSD board members, and the City of San Mateo Sustainability & 
Infrastructure Commission 
 
Save taxpayer money-removal would cost $1.3M+ and would jeopardize future grant funding 
 
Preserve safety- removing the middle section would create dangerous, disconnected bike lanes 
 
Further San Mateo’s commitment to Vision Zero made in 2015 and embedded into the City of San 
Mateo’s 2040 General Plan in 2024 
 
Please vote to prioritize safety and sustainable transportation in the City of San Mateo on February 2nd. 
 
 
Theresa Kong

​1/29/2026​
​City of San Mateo City Council​
​330 20th St, San Mateo, CA 94403​
​Copy to: SMFCSD Superintendent & SMFCSD Board of Trustees​
​Dear City of San Mateo City Council,​
​We are writing on behalf of the Parent Teacher Associations (PTA) of the San Mateo Foster City School District (SMFCSD). As​
​concerned leaders of our school community, we strongly support the preservation of safe bicycle lanes on Humboldt Street in​
​San Mateo. These lanes are essential for promoting Safe Routes to Schools and advancing the goals of Vision Zero.​
​Maintaining safe, accessible bicycle infrastructure is critical to the safety and well-being of our students and families, helping​
​to create a safer, more sustainable environment for all. We urge you to prioritize these efforts for the benefit of our entire​
​community.​
​The Humboldt Street bike lanes stretch 1.6 miles, making them one of the longest and most important segments of bicycle​
​infrastructure in the City of San Mateo. These lanes directly serve four schools, benefit all schools in the district, and provide a​
​crucial connection to downtown San Mateo and public transit. Their strategic location makes them an essential part of the​
​city's bicycle network. Additionally, the Humboldt Street bike lanes enable regional connectivity to the only safe bicycle​
​overpasses over Highway 101, linking the east and west sides of San Mateo, as well as providing bike routes to Foster City and​
​Burlingame. This network is vital for the safety and mobility of cyclists throughout the region.​
​We stand with the San Mateo community in expressing our concerns about pedestrian safety along Humboldt Street and in​
​the North Central neighborhood. We firmly believe it is possible to slow down vehicle traffic without compromising the​
​existing bicycle infrastructure. Safe Routes to Schools provide children with the opportunity to safely travel to school without​
​relying on cars, helping to reduce overall vehicle congestion. The City has a range of effective tools—such as speed monitoring,​
​increased patrols, speed bumps, and other measures that can be used to reduce vehicle speeds and enhance the safety of our​
​entire community.​
​One year ago, on February 1, 2024,​​SMFCSD PTA Presidents​​signed a letter advocating for the adoption of Vision Zero​.​​In that​
​letter, we stated: "Our cities can make infrastructure improvements, such as extended red curbing, additional stop signs and​
​crosswalks, bike lanes, and other solutions." Today, we are calling on the City to preserve the safe infrastructure of the​
​Humboldt Street bike lanes, which were installed in 2022. According to data from the City of San Mateo, these lanes are used​
​for over 10,000 bicycle trips per month.​​Removing​​the Humboldt Street bike lanes and forcing cyclists to share the road with​
​vehicle traffic would undermine the goals of Safe Routes to School and Vision Zero, compromising safety for all.​
​From our letter last year, also applicable in this case: “​Every student and their caregiver deserve​​peace of mind knowing their​
​child can safely travel to and from school.​”​
​Collectively we represent thousands of families in Foster City and San Mateo who want safer streets.​
​Sincerely,​
​Lauren Tsoi  1.16.2025​
​Sunnybrae Elementary PTA President, on behalf of the PTA Association​
​Shannon McGovern 1.22.2025​
​LEAD Elementary PTA President, on behalf of the PTA Association​

​Amy Connors 1.23.2025​
​Meadow Heights Elementary PTA President, on behalf of the PTA Association​
​Keshawn Womack 1.28.2025​

1
From:
Lisa Maley 
Sent:
Friday, January 30, 2026 2:33 PM
To:
City Council (San Mateo)
Subject:
Restore Humboldt Parking
 
Mayor Loraine and Councilmembers, 
 
 
I am writing as a resident of San Mateo to respectfully request that the City restore on-street 
parking along Humboldt Street. Since the removal of curb parking for the Humboldt bike lane 
project, day-to-day living for many households has become significantly more difficult. 
Residents, seniors, people with disabilities, families with young children, and our visitors now 
struggle to find reasonable parking near their homes. 
Even before the parking removal, this area already faced a tight parking supply due to older 
housing stock with limited off-street parking, multigenerational households, and high 
residential density. Eliminating large numbers of curb spaces on and around Humboldt has 
pushed those cars into surrounding streets forcing residents to circle multiple blocks or park 
far from home. This has increased tensions among neighbors, made it harder for caregivers 
and service providers to visit, and created safety concerns as people walk longer distances 
carrying children, groceries, or medical equipment. These impacts fall hardest on the most 
vulnerable residents.  
I also urge the City to carefully consider how it uses outside funding. Just because grant 
money is available for a particular design does not mean it is the right fit for this 
neighborhood, especially when it imposes serious burdens on existing residents. The 
possibility that the City might receive less grant funding in the future should not be used as a 
justification to deprive current residents of the basic, needed parking they rely on to access 
their homes, jobs, schools, and essential services. Grant programs should serve community 
needs, not drive decisions that undermine neighborhood livability. 
I recognize and support the City’s goals to improve bicycle safety and offer more sustainable 
transportation options. However, in a dense, older neighborhood with limited driveways and 
garages, major reductions in residential parking must be balanced against basic access needs 
for existing residents.  
Sincerely, 
Lisa Maley

Program intent: maximize availability of on-street parking for local residents

15 existing parking “zones”?

-​
# of permits per household 
-​
Current: unlimited plus 1 visitor per household 
-​
Council feedback: some limitation while “grandfathering” existing permit 
holders 
-​
New proposal: one permit per licensed driver w/ no household maximum 
-​
Program application & approval process 
-​
Current: review by staff & approval by PW director, mail-in vote of 
residents (one vote per residential household unit) 
-​
Council feedback: involve the S&I commission 
-​
New proposal: status quo + appeals to S&I commission + a “parking 
occupancy study” 
-​
Program removal or modification process 
-​
Current: resident request removal 
-​
Proposal: extend to include modifications 
-​
Parking “generators” 
-​
Current: schools, business, commercial districts or commercial uses 
-​

-​

unbundle their parking to then see residents all go and get free parking 
permits. But providing free curb parking is exactly why apartment 
buildings do not unbundle parking! 
-​
Permit issuance for corner properties 
-​
Current: corner lots are eligible 
-​
Proposal: corner lots are conditionally eligible 
-​
Future considerations: 
-​
Require residents to utilize off-street parking first 
-​
Proposal: don’t adopt, too confusing to enforce 
-​
New: online permit applications–permits mailed to them

From:

Subject:
On the Humboldt bike lanes
Attachments:
2019 San Mateo parking permit meeting.pdf
Dear City Council & CM Khojikian, 
As a daily bike lane user and new father, I'm writing to urge an exploration of a parking permit program for 
North Central. 
Removal of the bike lanes between Indian & Tilton would be a step backwards on the City Council's 
stated priority to build out a functioning bike network & would provide no meaningful parking respite to 
the neighborhood. 
The equity argument for removal misses a key point: equity priority communities are defined by high rates 
of zero-car households (MTC's definition).  
My neighbors I see using the bike lanes on Humboldt every day—predominantly day laborers commuting 
at all hours—are residents who depend on this infrastructure, not "rich people passing through."  
Removing these lanes directly harms the community members you have a moral responsibility protect. 
I understand parking concerns are real in North Central. The solution isn't eliminating bike 
infrastructure—it's reforming the parking permit program.  
In order to help inform future parking permitting conversations I've compiled an attached PDF of notes I 
took from the 2019 council discussion for your reference. 
A functional city needs both parking solutions AND safe bike infrastructure. These aren't competing 
priorities. 
Thank you for your service, 
 
Max Mautner

From:
Jon New 
Sent:
Saturday, January 31, 2026 12:26 AM
To:
City Council (San Mateo); Clerk; Nicole Fernandez
Subject:
Please keep the Humboldt St Bike Lanes
Dear Council, 
 
My name is Jonathan New, and I'm a homeowner in North Central. I'm strongly opposed to removing the 
Humboldt bike lanes. I'm sure you're going to hear a wide variety of perspectives. I would like to share 
two. 
 
First, I've been extremely disappointed in the lack of progress, or even discussion, on a residential 
parking permit program. Despite attending meetings and reviewing available materials, I am not aware of 
any concrete proposals. When I raised this issue with staff, I was told permits are “inequitable” and 
“unwelcoming.” But, failing to manage demand for scarce parking resources is neither equitable nor 
effective. Many cities successfully use permit systems with guest passes and income-based 
adjustments. Parking management should be addressed directly, not by removing safety infrastructure.
 
Second, and most importantly, we know bike lanes make streets safer for cyclists and pedestrians. 
There are countless studies that demonstrate this. This is not speculative policy; it's consistently 
supported with real-world data. At the risk of sounding melodramatic, are we really considering spending 
hundreds of thousands during a fiscal budget crunch to make a street less safe? Especially during a year 
where we've already seen multiple pedestrian fatalities?  
 
I urge the Council to keep the Humboldt bike lanes and continue iterating on improvements that enhance 
safety for everyone who uses our streets. 
 
Thank you for your time and consideration. 
 
Jonathan New 
San Mateo
