Humboldt bike lanes

Dear Mayor Lorraine, Deputy Mayor Fernandez and the San Mateo City Council:

| am writing on behalf of San Mateo Forward. We have 57 dues-paying members in the City
of San Mateo.

San Mateo Forward asks the Council to vote against any proposal that removes any portion
of the bike lanes on Humboldt Street. The bike lanes provide safety and connectivity to the
residents of North Central, San Mateo, and neighboring cities. This includes many low
income, people of color who are unable to afford a car to safely get to work or shuttle their
kids to the many schools on Humboldt.

North Central is already a dense and walkable neighborhood. It attracts many new, young
families to San Mateo given its proximity to downtown, Caltrain, and Samtrans. When we
build and maintain safe bike infrastructure, more people bike and we attract new residents
who are less car dependent. The result is safer streets, less congestion, higher quality of
life, more visually attractive spaces, and higher property values. If we are serious about
meeting our housing goals and making housing more affordable in San Mateo, we cannot
continue to adopt policies that encourage ownership of 3+ vehicles and dependence on
taxpayer supported free car storage. Keep in mind that North Central already has 5,882

other projects that will help increase housing affordability in San Mateo.

From:
Kolja Schluetter 
Sent:
Friday, January 30, 2026 9:47 AM
To:
Clerk; City Council (San Mateo)
Subject:
Humboldt Bike Lanes and Fiscal Responsibility
Good morning Council Members, 
  
I just read the recent San Mateo Daily Journal op-ed by Mr. Swire regarding the Humboldt Street bike 
lanes and their implications for San Mateo taxpayers. 
https://www.smdailyjournal.com/opinion/letters to editor/removing-bike-lanes-will-cost-san-mateo-
taxpayers/article_7e2636e2-e2bb-411b-affa-f496465bdc4a.html 
  
I do not live in North Central, and I genuinely empathize with residents who may feel they were 
insufficiently engaged during the initial decision-making process. That said, I believe Mr. Swire is correct 
on the central issue he's raising in the op-ed: It would be fiscally irresponsible to remove functioning 
safety infrastructure at significant cost to taxpayers, particularly at a time when the City’s financial 
outlook is strained and new tax increases are being contemplated. 
  
This concern is amplified by the fact that removing recently installed bike lanes would likely invite 
significantly increased scrutiny of San Mateo’s future applications for state and federal infrastructure 
grants. Reversing completed projects weakens the City’s credibility as a responsible steward of public 
funds and risks jeopardizing future outside funding for transportation and safety improvements. 
  
In principle, I support raising taxes to fund necessary infrastructure improvements when they are truly 
needed. However, I cannot support tax increases while the City simultaneously considers/approves 
spending millions of dollars to actively dismantle recently installed public safety infrastructure. That 
approach undermines public trust and suggests a lack of fiscal discipline. 
  
If the City is serious about long-term infrastructure overhauls and responsible financial stewardship, 
Council should follow the recommendation of the Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission and vote 
to keep the Humboldt bike lanes in place. If austerity is required, it should begin with avoiding wasteful 
reversals, not with asking residents to pay more while functional infrastructure is torn out. 
  
Thank you for your consideration. 
 
Best, Kolja Schluetter

Dear Mayor Lorraine and SM City Council,
Please do not remove the new bike lanes around San Mateo High, College Park/Fiesta
Gardens Elementary, and San Mateo Adult Schools - the most dangerous streets in the City.
We need to make our streets safer for kids who walk and bike so that we can reduce the
increasing number of fatalities and the traffic congestion that plague our streets.

school, recreate, or commute in the area.  Bike lanes:
-  Save lives for kids and parents who bike

pollution
-  Increase property values
-  Make our streets more beautiful
-  Create a sense of community and and encourage people to shop locally
-  Reduce taxpayer expenses through lower road maintenance and public health spending
-  Facilitate safe, low cost travel for those unable to afford the skyrocketing cost of car

RESOLUTION NO. 10/24-25

RESOLUTION OF THE BOARD OF EDUCATION
OF THE SAN MATEO-FOSTER CITY SCHOOL DISTRICT
IN SUPPORT OF THE PRESERVATION OF SAFE BICYCLE LANES
ON HUMBOLDT STREET IN SAN MATEO

WHEREAS, it is of utmost importance that we address the critical need to maintain safe and
accessible bicycle infrastructure within our community.

Meanwhile, ensuring our students’ and families' safety and well-being is paramount to creating a
sustainable and secure environment for all individuals.

WHEREAS, the Humboldt Street bike lanes, stretching 1.6 miles, stand as one of the longest and
most vital segments of bicycle infrastructure in the City of San Mateo. These lanes serve four
schools directly, benefitting the entire schoo! district community, and provide a crucial link to
downtown San Mateo and public transportation.

WHEREAS, the strategic location of these bike lanes makes them an important component of the
city's bicycle network. This network enables regional connectivity to safe bicycle overpasses over
Highway 101, connects the east and west sides of San Mateo, and provides bike routes to Foster
City and Burlingame. It plays a vital role in ensuring the safety and mobility of cyclists throughout
the region.

WHEREAS, we express our concerns regarding pedestrian safety along Humboldt Street and in the
North Central neighborhood. We firmly believe in slowing down vehicle traffic without compromising
existing bicycle infrastructure.

WHEREAS, Safe Routes to Schools offers students the opportunity to commute to school safely,
minimizing reliance on cars and reducing overall vehicle congestion. We believe that the City of San
Mateo possesses an array of effective tools that can be implemented to decrease vehicle speeds
and enhance the safety of our entire community.

WHEREAS, we strongly recommend that the City of San Mateo take immediate action to preserve
the safe infrastructure of the Humboldt Street bike lanes, which were diligently installed in 2022.
The recent City of San Mateo data reveals that these lanes are a crucial transportation route for
over 10,000 monthly bicycle trips.

WHEREAS, efforts to remove the Humboldt Street bike lanes and impose a shared space with
vehicle traffic would be detrimental to the objectives of Safe Routes to School and pose a significant
threat to the overall safety and well-being of all individuals utilizing these routes.

NOW THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, we urge the San Mateo City Council to maintain the
integrity of the Humboldt Street bike lanes for the benefit of our community. Your attention to this
matter and subsequent support in preserving these vital transportation routes will undoubtedly
enhance safety and accessibility for all residents.

ADOPTED, SIGNED, AND APPROVED this 23rd day of January 2025.

299 of 368

1
From:
Mari 
Sent:
Saturday, January 31, 2026 9:15 AM
To:
Danielle Cwirko-Godycki; Nicole Fernandez; Adam Loraine; Rob Newsom; Lisa Diaz Nash
Cc:
Clerk; City Council (San Mateo)
Subject:
I Support Keeping the Humboldt Bike Lane AS IS
To the City Council, 
I’m writing as a North Central parent and resident to ask you to protect and maintain the Humboldt 
Street bike lane exactly as it is. Two-thirds of community members surveyed, even those who live on 
Humboldt itself, support keeping the lane intact. That should carry weight. 
As the weather improves, my family uses this lane more and more. My kids ride it to elementary school, I 
use it to commute by bike to my job in Burlingame, and my in-laws—who are in their mid 70s, don’t drive, 
and live south of downtown—use it to visit us and pick up our kids from school. We rely on this 
infrastructure. 
It’s frustrating to hear claims that the bike lane “isn’t successful” when the city never completed the full 
network or promoted its use. If we only implement parts of a plan, of course the outcome will fall short. 
That doesn’t mean the plan failed—it means we didn’t finish the work. 
And frankly, I can’t understand how parking spots and convenience are being elevated above basic 
safety. Do we value cleaner air? Then we need more bikes. Do we want kids to move freely and 
independently, not just sit in cars? Then we need more bikes. Do we want a connected, livable 
community? Then we need more bikes. 
If that’s our goal, we must connect the lanes. Build more of them. Promote them. Create city-led rides 
and safety campaigns. Show people how to use this infrastructure—not blame them when it’s still new 
and incomplete. 
At a previous meeting, I heard people say they can’t walk groceries from a few blocks away. But why not 
unload groceries at your driveway and then park? Yes, it may take a few extra minutes and a little bit of 
walking. It might even improve our health. Meanwhile, people are getting hit on our streets. We can do 
better than this. 
Please don’t reverse a public investment that’s already improving safety. Move forward, not backward—
with leadership that reflects the city we want to become. 
With hope and respect, 
Mariana Tiwari 
North Central

1
From:
Connie Weiss 
Sent:
Saturday, January 31, 2026 12:14 PM
To:
City Council (San Mateo)
Subject:
February 2, 2026 Agenda Item 7: Humboldt Bike Lanes Alternative - Update
Honorable San Mateo City Council Members, 
The February 2nd City Council agenda includes an item which will determine who has more influence 
with City Council: well-funded special interests or the voices of residents. 
In February 2022, residents of North Central, an Equity Priority Neighborhood, were clear: bike lanes 
on Humboldt were not an issue if parking was not removed. Ms.Trina Pierce presented the 2022 City 
Council a petition signed by 748 residents objecting to removal of street parking. That night, the City 
Council ignored the voices of residents and voted to establish the bike lanes. 
The Community Development Block Grant Program (CDBG) grant funding was clearly provided to 
improve the North Central and Shoreview neighborhoods with much needed street lighting, sidewalk 
repairs, and repairs to the Martin Luther King Center, among other items, that would directly benefit 
North Central and Shoreview residents. Installing bike lanes was not listed in the grant. 
North Central and Shoreview saw little or no improvements resulting from the grant funding. The 
funds intended for improvements that would directly benefit the community were spent to provide 
little-used and unsafe bike lanes. The grant funding certainly was not awarded to create a power-play 
between well-funded bicycle special interest groups and the residents of a neighborhood who are 
simply trying to get by. 
From 2022 to 2025, there were periodic, aggressive and loud demands by people aligned with bicycle 
special interests and the muted voices of real residents of North Central whose lives have been 
greatly impacted by the bike lanes. Then, in February 2025, the current City Council discussed and 
adopted a plan to restore parking to Humboldt and to look for other alternatives for bike lanes. 
Residents were elated. We felt we now had a Council that respects resident voices. We looked 
forward to the staff findings and report. 
During the December 2025 meeting of the Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission, it was clear 
just a few minutes into the City staff’s presentation about the Humboldt bike lanes that something had 
gone horribly wrong. The data reported was ridiculously inconsistent with what residents, and resident 
bike ride surveys, were reporting. The objections by residents were ignored in staff’s presentation, it 
was as if they did not exist. Those who had been so vocal at every in-person meeting conducted by 
staff were essentially treated as being non-existent. 
Residents, busy with their lives and tired of repeating themselves for almost three years, spoke during 
public comment, but they were far outnumbered by the well-financed special interests who attended 
the meeting. Once again, the residents of North Central, many of whom are economically challenged, 
minorities, elderly and disabled who live in a recognized Equity Priority Neighborhood were treated as 
second-class citizens. The Council directive of “restore parking” was gone. 
305 of 368

2
From this “gone sideways” December 2025 meeting, you are now being presented with a 
recommendation that was not an option in the February 2025 Alternative vote made by Council. 
Whether City staff realizes it or not, their data, reporting, and recommendation has been significantly 
skewed to favor the well-funded special interests and, as in 2022, ignore the voices of residents. Staff 
discarded what was believed to be duplicate returns to their web survey. No more proof that the 
survey was flawed and manipulated is needed, period. It needs to be thrown out.

used. Many resident bikers have spoken up about the dangerous conditions on Humboldt,

without the green paint on the road. Although Crystal Springs Road is a designated bike route, I see

sense and safety combined, and so easy to make a reality!

working-class people who are just trying to live their lives, with your vote. 
Will you follow the misguided recommendation of staff, fully aligned with special interests, or 
will you stand firm on the direction given to staff to come up with a plan to fully restore 
parking now and then determine alternative routes for bikes?

1
From:
Wayne Young 
Sent:
Thursday, January 29, 2026 8:26 PM
To:
City Council (San Mateo)
Subject:
Support Retaining the Humboldt Street Bike Lanes — Consistent with San Mateo 
General Plan 2040 and Bicycle Master Plan
Dear Members of the San Mateo City Council, 
I am writing to respectfully request that the City of San Mateo retain the existing bike lanes on 
Humboldt Street, consistent with the City’s adopted planning priorities — including the General Plan 
2040 and the Bicycle Master Plan. 
San Mateo’s General Plan 2040 establishes a citywide vision for a multimodal transportation system 
that is safe, accessible, equitable, and sustainable. The General Plan explicitly states goals and 
policies to prioritize walking, bicycling, and transit, to reduce reliance on single-occupancy vehicles, 
lower greenhouse gas emissions, and expand transportation choices for all residents regardless of age 
or ability. Policies such as C-1.1 (Sustainable Transportation)and C-1.2 (Complete Streets) emphasize 
designing streets that facilitate safe, comfortable, and efficient travel for people bicycling as a core 
component of the circulation network. In addition, the General Plan includes a specific goal (Goal C-4) 
to build and maintain a safe, connected, and equitable bicycle network that provides access to key 
community destinations like employment centers, transit, schools, and shopping.  
These priorities are mirrored in San Mateo’s Bicycle Master Plan, which identifies the Humboldt Street 
bike lanes as part of an essential connected bike network. The Master Plan was adopted after 
community engagement and data-driven analysis and serves as the official blueprint for bicycle 
infrastructure in the city. It prioritizes improvements that make streets safer and more predictable for 
people choosing to bike.  
Retaining the Humboldt Street bike lanes — rather than removing them — reflects the intent of both 
plans by providing safer infrastructure for everyday trips like commuting, getting to schools, and 
accessing local businesses. The bike lanes help advance multiple adopted City goals: 
 
Safety: Dedicated bike lanes reduce conflicts between people biking and people driving, support 
a Vision Zero approach, and help prevent injuries and fatalities.  
 
Equity & Access: Many North Central residents depend on bicycling and other active modes to 
reach schools, jobs, transit, and services without access to a car. A robust bike network expands 
mobility choices for all income levels and ages.  
 
Sustainability & Climate: Increasing bicycle mode share supports San Mateo’s goals to reduce 
vehicle miles traveled and transportation emissions while improving public health through active 
transportation.  
While concerns about parking and neighborhood needs deserve thoughtful engagement, removing 
infrastructure that aligns with the City’s own long-range planning priorities would undermine years of 
community input and data analysis embedded in the General Plan 2040 and the Bicycle Master Plan. 
312 of 368

--- page 313 ---
2
I encourage you to retain the Humboldt Street bike lanes and pursue targeted refinements — such as 
traffic calming, safety improvements, and parking mitigation where appropriate — that keep San Mateo 
moving toward the goals our community has already formally adopted. 
Thank you for your careful consideration and for your continued service to our city. 
Sincerely, 
Wayne Young 
San Mateo North Central Resident

Subject:
Comment for Agenda Item 7, Humboldt Bike Lanes Alternative
Dear Mayor and City Councilmembers, 
 
I'm Rick Ballard, a North Central resident. I care deeply about my neighborhood and my neighbors. And 
I'm writing to ask you to keep the Humboldt bike lanes. 
 
I want to focus on two things. 
 
First, the proposed alternatives are dangerous — not because of speed, but because of sightlines. 
On streets like Fremont, a driver pulling out of a driveway cannot see an oncoming cyclist until it's too 
late. I've experienced this; a driver came out of a driveway, couldn't see me, and I missed being hit by 
barely a foot. Speed humps won't fix this. Traffic circles won't fix this. The streets are narrow, driveways 
are everywhere, and the geometry doesn't change. This is the same sightline problem that killed a four-
year-old in Burlingame this year. 
 
If you reroute cyclists — including children biking to school — down these streets, someone will be 
seriously hurt or killed. I don't want that to be this council's legacy. 
 
Second, this is fiscal recklessness. The city is running a budget deficit. You are preparing to ask voters 
for a tax increase. And you are considering spending over a million dollars to rip out recently-installed 
infrastructure and restore parking spaces. It's hard to ask citizens for more money while spending this 
way. 
 
Please keep the Humboldt Street bike lanes. 
 
Thank you, 
Rick Ballard 
North Central San Mateo resident

ride on or cross the Humboldt bike lane. I’m one of many. Humboldt street is challenging with both high 
speed and high volume traffic. The Humboldt  bike lanes importantly provides a safer, more predictable 
street for people of all ages who choose to bike, walk, or drive. Removing them would reduce safety and 
accessibility, not improve it. 
I’ve heard concerns raised about parking and older residents. These are important issues, but they 
deserve solutions that don’t come at the expense of safety, sustainability, and long-term livability. Many 
older residents benefit directly from calmer streets, safer crossings, and reduced traffic speeds, 
outcomes that bike lanes help deliver. 
San Mateo has the opportunity to continue moving toward a more walkable, livable city that supports a 
variety of transportation choices. I strongly encourage you to keep the Humboldt Street bike lanes and 
focus on improving, rather than undoing, our existing infrastructure. 
Thank you for your consideration.

Ce: Clerk; City Council (San Mateo); Andrew Reback
Subject: Bike lanes and resident safety

Dear Council,

We’ve had multiple pedestrian deaths within a few miles of my house in just the last few months. That’s a
signal our street system is not safe enough. When people are being killed, the response should be to
strengthen safety measures, not remove them.

Bike lanes are not just for cyclists. They slow vehicle speeds, make movement more predictable, and
shorten crossing distances for pedestrians. Speed is the biggest factor in whether someone Survives a
crash.

This is bigger than Humboldt. San Mateo is growing, and our streets have to work for kids walking to
school, older adults crossing the street, and people biking or using mobility devices. Design matters
more than enforcement. When roads feel wide and fast, drivers go fast. When streets are designed to be
calmer, people survive.

Many cities around us, including Burlingame, are moving toward MORE experimentation and people-
focused street designs. That reflects where urban safety practice is headed. San Mateo should be
moving forward with that progress, and NOT stepping backward.

Removing a bike lane after tragedies moves us in the wrong direction. Please keep the Humboldt bike
lane and continue prioritizing street designs that protect human life first.

Thank you,

Andrew Reback (Alice Cathcart, Elliott Reback, Beatrice Reback)

D1/North Central

2/2/26 Humboldt Bike Lane Relocation
Mayor Loraine and Councilmembers - You're going to hear a lot of noise tonight, and no doubt have 
already received tons of AI generated emails, form letters, and communications of all sorts decrying the 
outrageous removal of the bike lanes on Humboldt. Many of these will be from people who do not live on 
Humboldt, in North Central, the surrounding neighborhoods, San Mateo, or even the Bay Area or state. 
Your job is to separate the signal from this noise. 
 
Most if not all of you would say you like to be "data-driven". Let's focus on that, because the data 
illustrates several things: these lanes are simply not used. We have camera data, data from another 
citizen who put out cameras, and personally I drive that corridor up to 4x a day between here and 
Burlingame High School with my son, and my observations corroborate that complete lack of usage. 
There are usually literally zero bikes - commute hours, school hours, beautiful weather, weekdays, 
weekends - doesn't matter. Secondly, the removal of parking has negatively impacted an equity priority 
neighborhood with seniors, and workers that rely on vehicles to make a living. Finally, the lanes have 
been in place for over 2 years, and there is no data to suggest it has made anything safer - there has been 
no decrease (or increase) in collisions. That makes sense because if you have zero usage, you will also 
have zero collisions. 
 
In a nutshell - the suffering being endured by the residents of North Central on this corridor is being 
inflicted for no good reason. None. 
 
It's worth noting as well that no one is removing lanes - they city will simply relocate them to better 
places. Also worth noting these lanes were rushed to be installed without proper neighborhood 
notification and meetings that would have avoided this disaster in the first place. So this is really righting 
a wrong that should never have occured. 
 
As an avid cyclist with 10s of thousands of miles ridden everywhere imaginable - big cities, small cities, 
on road, off road, foreign countries - I can tell you we don't generally care about bike lines. Even when I 
bike with my wife and kids, we find side streets and go the most expeditiious yet safe routes. I only bike 
ECR when absolutely necessary, and I avoid Delaware. For the same reason, Humboldt is sub-optimal as 
a truck route and main thoroughfare. We also don't mind going a little further for a nicer, quieter ride - it's 
easy on a bike. 
 
Also as a cyclist I'm embarrassed by the bike zealots and their antics. They do not represent me nor do I 
believe they represent the majority of cyclists. Again, many of these people don't live in the affected area, 
much less San Mateo, and I promise you they do not really use these lanes, since nobody really does. It's 
also sad to see the "Safe Streets Everywhere" (funded by the same large bike coalition SVBC) being 
weaponized as a means to justify the theft of parking from these residents under the guise of safety (who 
are these phantom riders being kept safe?), rather than representing the actual residents of San Mateo. 
Don’t reward the tantrums of this handful of zealots with your support.

and relocating these lanes on safety is zero. The net impact on the residents who had their parking

So, you find yourself in the difficult position of being villainized by outsiders, oftentimes with highly

❑Appreciate the speed calming measures 
for both alternatives, but still view the 
alternatives as a downgrade from the 
existing Class II on Humboldt Street

increase existing lighting 
levels are well supported
The community is 
supportive for measures 
to slow speeds and 
volumes in neighborhood 
streets, but not at the 
trade-off of removing 
parking or existing bicycle 
infrastructure

all three survey formats 
preferred to keep the bike 
lanes on Humboldt Street 
(400+ surveys received)

indicated residents living on 
Humboldt and Idaho Street 
preferred the Fremont Street 
Bike Boulevard Alternative over 
retaining the Humboldt Street 
bike lanes

problem for the North Central 
community-specifically for 
residents on Humboldt Street, 
where parking spaces were 
removed for the installation 
of the bike lanes

Alternative 1 
Keep As-Is
• Existing Facility: Keep existing Class II bicycle facility on Humboldt street
• Parking on Humboldt Street: Parking on Humboldt Street from 2nd Avenue to 
Indian Avenue will not be restored
$0
Alternative 2 
Keep As-Is with Additional 
Humboldt Street Calming 
Measures + Streetlighting 
Upgrades + 
Explore Permit Parking Program
• Existing Facility: Keep existing Class II bicycle facility on Humboldt street
• Parking on Humboldt Street: Parking on Humboldt Street from 2nd Avenue to 
Indian Avenue will not be restored
• Streetlighting: Streetlighting on Humboldt Street from Peninsula Avenue to 5th 
Avenue will be upgraded to a brighter fixture
• Other 
• Staff will explore a tailored permit parking program for North Central to 
address the Humboldt bike lanes impacts

Humboldt Street to slow speeds on Humboldt Street

--- page 362 ---
Potential Alternatives – 3 and 4
Alternative 
Summary
Estimated 
Cost: 
Alternative 3
Idaho Street Bike Boulevard 
+ 
Streetlighting Upgrades
• Existing Facility: Remove keep existing Class II bicycle facility on Humboldt street 
(Indian Ave. to 2nd Ave.)
• New Facility: Install a new bicycle boulevard on Idaho Street from 2nd avenue to 
Indian Avenue per the final Idaho Street Alternative
• Parking on Humboldt Street: Parking on Humboldt Street from 2nd Avenue to 
Indian Avenue will be restored (approximately 100 parking spaces)
• Streetlighting: Streetlighting will be upgraded for Idaho Street per the limits of 
the bicycle boulevard and on Humboldt Street from Peninsula Ave. to 5th Ave.
• HUD CDBG Funding: Will need to repay HUD for removed bicycle facilities 
$1.773M
Alternative 4
Fremont Street Bike Boulevard 
+ 
Streetlighting Upgrades
• Existing Facility: Remove keep existing Class II bicycle facility on Humboldt street 
(Indian Ave. to 2nd Ave.)
• New Facility: Install a new bicycle boulevard on Fremont Street from 2nd avenue 
to Indian Avenue per the final Fremont Street Alternative
• Parking on Humboldt Street: Parking on Humboldt Street from 2nd Avenue to 
Indian Avenue will be restored (approximately 100 parking spaces)
• Streetlighting: Streetlighting will be upgraded for Idaho Street per the limits of 
the bicycle boulevard and on Humboldt Street from Peninsula Ave. to 5th Ave.
• HUD CDBG Funding: Will need to repay HUD for removed bicycle facilities 
$1.733M
